<p id="mwGQ"><b id="mwGg">Reptiles</b>, as most commonly defined,<!-- We are not employing the cladistic definition in the common definition of reptile --> are the animals in the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Class_(biology)" title="Class (biology)" id="mwGw">class</a> <b id="mwHA">Reptilia</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap" about="#mwt16" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"IPAc-en","href":"./Template:IPAc-en"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"r"},"2":{"wt":"E"},"3":{"wt":"p"},"4":{"wt":"&apos;"},"5":{"wt":"t"},"6":{"wt":"I"},"7":{"wt":"l"},"8":{"wt":"i"},"9":{"wt":"ə"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwHQ"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key" about="#mwt17" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"respell","href":"./Template:Respell"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"rep"},"2":{"wt":"TIL"},"3":{"wt":"ee"},"4":{"wt":"ə"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwHg"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">rep-<span style="font-size:90%">TIL</span>-ee-ə</i></a>), a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Paraphyletic" title="Paraphyletic" class="mw-redirect" id="mwHw">paraphyletic</a> grouping comprising all <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sauropsid" title="Sauropsid" class="mw-redirect" id="mwIA">sauropsids</a> except <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Birds" title="Birds" class="mw-redirect" id="mwIQ">birds</a>.<sup about="#mwt18" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Gauthier-1994-Prothero-Schoch_1-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Gauthier-1994-Prothero-Schoch"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Gauthier-1994-Prothero-Schoch-1" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 1;" id="mwIg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwIw">[1]</span></a></sup> Living reptiles comprise <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Turtle" title="Turtle" id="mwJA">turtles</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crocodilia" title="Crocodilia" id="mwJQ">crocodilians</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Squamata" title="Squamata" id="mwJg">squamates</a> (<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lizard" title="Lizard" id="mwJw">lizards</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Snake" title="Snake" id="mwKA">snakes</a>) and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Rhynchocephalia" title="Rhynchocephalia" id="mwKQ">rhynchocephalians</a> (<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Tuatara" title="Tuatara" id="mwKg">tuatara</a>). As of March 2022, the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Reptile_Database" title="Reptile Database" id="mwKw">Reptile Database</a> includes about 11,700<span typeof="mw:Entity" id="mwLA"> </span>species.<sup about="#mwt22" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-2"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-2" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 2;" id="mwLQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwLg">[2]</span></a></sup> In the traditional <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Linnaean_taxonomy" title="Linnaean taxonomy" id="mwLw">Linnaean</a> classification system, birds are considered a separate class to reptiles. However, crocodilians are more closely related to birds than they are to other living reptiles, and so modern <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cladistics" title="Cladistics" id="mwMA">cladistic</a> classification systems include birds within Reptilia, redefining the term as a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Clade" title="Clade" id="mwMQ">clade</a>. Other cladistic definitions abandon the term reptile altogether in favor of the clade <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sauropsida" title="Sauropsida" id="mwMg">Sauropsida</a>, which refers to all amniotes more closely related to modern reptiles than to mammals. The study of the traditional reptile <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Order_(biology)" title="Order (biology)" id="mwMw">orders</a>, customarily in combination with the study of modern <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Amphibian" title="Amphibian" id="mwNA">amphibians</a>, is called <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Herpetology" title="Herpetology" id="mwNQ">herpetology</a>.</p>

<p id="mwNg">The earliest known proto-reptiles originated around 312 million years ago during the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Carboniferous" title="Carboniferous" id="mwNw">Carboniferous</a> period, having evolved from advanced <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Reptiliomorpha" title="Reptiliomorpha" id="mwOA">reptiliomorph</a> tetrapods which became increasingly adapted to life on dry land. The earliest known <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Eureptilia" title="Eureptilia" id="mwOQ">eureptile</a> ("true reptile") was <i id="mwOg"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Hylonomus" title="Hylonomus" id="mwOw">Hylonomus</a>,</i> a small and superficially lizard-like animal. Genetic and fossil data argues that the two largest lineages of reptiles, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Archosauromorpha" title="Archosauromorpha" id="mwPA">Archosauromorpha</a> (crocodilians, birds, and kin) and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lepidosauromorpha" title="Lepidosauromorpha" id="mwPQ">Lepidosauromorpha</a> (lizards, and kin), diverged near the end of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Permian" title="Permian" id="mwPg">Permian</a> period.<sup about="#mwt27" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-3" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-3"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-3" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 3;" id="mwPw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwQA">[3]</span></a></sup> In addition to the living reptiles, there are many diverse groups that are now <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Extinction" title="Extinction" id="mwQQ">extinct</a>, in some cases due to <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Extinction_event" title="Extinction event" id="mwQg">mass extinction events</a>. In particular, the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cretaceous–Paleogene_extinction_event" title="Cretaceous–Paleogene extinction event" id="mwQw">Cretaceous–Paleogene extinction event</a> wiped out the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pterosaur" title="Pterosaur" id="mwRA">pterosaurs</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Plesiosauria" title="Plesiosauria" class="mw-redirect" id="mwRQ">plesiosaurs</a>, and all non-avian <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dinosaurs" title="Dinosaurs" class="mw-redirect" id="mwRg">dinosaurs</a> alongside many species of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crocodyliformes" title="Crocodyliformes" id="mwRw">crocodyliforms</a>, and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Squamata" title="Squamata" id="mwSA">squamates</a> (e.g., <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mosasaur" title="Mosasaur" id="mwSQ">mosasaurs</a>). Modern non-bird reptiles inhabit all the continents except <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Antarctica" title="Antarctica" id="mwSg">Antarctica</a>.</p>

<p id="mwSw">Reptiles are tetrapod <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vertebrates" title="Vertebrates" class="mw-redirect" id="mwTA">vertebrates</a>, creatures that either have four limbs or, like snakes, are descended from four-limbed ancestors. Unlike <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Amphibian" title="Amphibian" id="mwTQ">amphibians</a>, reptiles do not have an aquatic larval stage. Most reptiles are <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Oviparous" title="Oviparous" class="mw-redirect" id="mwTg">oviparous</a>, although several species of squamates are <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Viviparity" title="Viviparity" id="mwTw">viviparous</a>, as were some extinct aquatic clades<sup about="#mwt35" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-S12_4-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"S12"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-S12-4"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-S12-4" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 4;" id="mwUA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwUQ">[4]</span></a></sup>  – the fetus develops within the mother, using a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Placentation#In_lizards_and_snakes" title="Placentation" id="mwUg">(non-mammalian) placenta</a> rather than contained in an <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Eggshell" title="Eggshell" id="mwUw">eggshell</a>. As amniotes, reptile eggs are surrounded by membranes for protection and transport, which adapt them to reproduction on dry land. Many of the viviparous species feed their <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Fetus" title="Fetus" id="mwVA">fetuses</a> through various forms of placenta analogous to those of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mammal" title="Mammal" id="mwVQ">mammals</a>, with some providing initial care for their hatchlings. <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Neontology" title="Neontology" id="mwVg">Extant</a> reptiles range in size from a tiny gecko, <i id="mwVw"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sphaerodactylus_ariasae" title="Sphaerodactylus ariasae" id="mwWA">Sphaerodactylus ariasae</a></i>, which can grow up to <span about="#mwt29" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"convert","href":"./Template:Convert"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"17"},"2":{"wt":"mm"},"3":{"wt":"in"},"4":{"wt":"1"},"abbr":{"wt":"on"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwWQ">17</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt29"> </span><span about="#mwt29">mm (0.7</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt29"> </span><span about="#mwt29">in)</span> to the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Saltwater_crocodile" title="Saltwater crocodile" id="mwWg">saltwater crocodile</a>, <i id="mwWw">Crocodylus porosus</i>, which can reach over <span about="#mwt30" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"convert","href":"./Template:Convert"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"6"},"2":{"wt":"m"},"3":{"wt":"ft"},"4":{"wt":"1"},"abbr":{"wt":"on"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwXA">6</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt30"> </span><span about="#mwt30">m (19.7</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt30"> </span><span about="#mwt30">ft)</span> in length and weigh over <span about="#mwt31" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"convert","href":"./Template:Convert"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"1000"},"2":{"wt":"kg"},"3":{"wt":"lb"},"abbr":{"wt":"on"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwXQ">1,000</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt31"> </span><span about="#mwt31">kg (2,200</span><span typeof="mw:Entity" about="#mwt31"> </span><span about="#mwt31">lb)</span>.</p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="1" id="mwXg"><h2 id="Classification">Classification</h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt36" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"see also","href":"./Template:See_also"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"List of reptiles"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwXw"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt36" id="mwYA">See also: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./List_of_reptiles" title="List of reptiles">List of reptiles</a></div>

<section data-mw-section-id="2" id="mwYQ"><h3 id="Research_history">Research history</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt39" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"See also","href":"./Template:See_also"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Skull roof"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwYg"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt39" id="mwYw">See also: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Skull_roof" title="Skull roof">Skull roof</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwZA"><a href="./File:Reptile003d.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwZQ"><img resource="./File:Reptile003d.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Reptile003d.jpg/220px-Reptile003d.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="9604" data-file-height="13600" data-file-type="bitmap" height="312" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Reptile003d.jpg/330px-Reptile003d.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Reptile003d.jpg/440px-Reptile003d.jpg 2x" id="mwZg"/></a><figcaption id="mwZw">Reptiles, from <i id="mwaA">Nouveau Larousse Illustré</i>, 1897–1904, notice the inclusion of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Amphibian" title="Amphibian" id="mwaQ">amphibians</a> (below the crocodiles)</figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwag">In the 13th century the category of <i id="mwaw">reptile</i> was recognized in Europe as consisting of a miscellany of egg-laying creatures, including "snakes, various fantastic monsters, lizards, assorted amphibians, and worms", as recorded by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vincent_of_Beauvais" title="Vincent of Beauvais" id="mwbA">Beauvais</a> in his <i id="mwbQ">Mirror of Nature</i>.<sup about="#mwt46" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-5" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-5"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-5" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 5;" id="mwbg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwbw">[5]</span></a></sup>
In the 18th century, the reptiles were, from the outset of classification, grouped with the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Amphibian" title="Amphibian" id="mwcA">amphibians</a>. <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Carl_Linnaeus" title="Carl Linnaeus" id="mwcQ">Linnaeus</a>, working from species-poor <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sweden" title="Sweden" id="mwcg">Sweden</a>, where the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Common_adder" title="Common adder" class="mw-redirect" id="mwcw">common adder</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Grass_snake" title="Grass snake" id="mwdA">grass snake</a> are often found hunting in water, included all reptiles and amphibians in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Class_(biology)" title="Class (biology)" id="mwdQ">class</a> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Amphibia_in_the_10th_edition_of_Systema_Naturae" title="Amphibia in the 10th edition of Systema Naturae" id="mwdg"><span class="nowrap" about="#mwt52" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"nobr","href":"./Template:Nobr"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"\"III – Amphibia\""}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwdw">"III – Amphibia"</span></a> in his <i id="mweA"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Systema_Naturæ" title="Systema Naturæ" class="mw-redirect" id="mweQ">Systema Naturæ</a></i>.<sup about="#mwt51" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Linn1758_6-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Linn1758"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Linn1758-6"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Linn1758-6" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 6;" id="mweg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwew">[6]</span></a></sup>
The terms <i id="mwfA">reptile</i> and <i id="mwfQ">amphibian</i> were largely interchangeable, <i id="mwfg">reptile</i> (from Latin <i id="mwfw">repere</i>, 'to creep') being preferred by the French.<sup about="#mwt58" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-7" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-7"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-7" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 7;" id="mwgA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwgQ">[7]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Josephus_Nicolaus_Laurenti" title="Josephus Nicolaus Laurenti" id="mwgg">J.N. Laurenti</a> was the first to formally use the term <i id="mwgw">Reptilia</i> for an expanded selection of reptiles and amphibians basically similar to that of Linnaeus.<sup about="#mwt62" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-8" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-8"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-8" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 8;" id="mwhA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwhQ">[8]</span></a></sup> Today, the two groups are still commonly treated under the single heading <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Herpetology" title="Herpetology" id="mwhg">herpetology</a>.</p>

<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwhw"><a href="./File:MosasaurDiscovery.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwiA"><img resource="./File:MosasaurDiscovery.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MosasaurDiscovery.jpg/220px-MosasaurDiscovery.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="1836" data-file-height="845" data-file-type="bitmap" height="101" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MosasaurDiscovery.jpg/330px-MosasaurDiscovery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/MosasaurDiscovery.jpg/440px-MosasaurDiscovery.jpg 2x" id="mwiQ"/></a><figcaption id="mwig">"Antediluvian monster", a <i id="mwiw"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mosasaurus" title="Mosasaurus" id="mwjA">Mosasaurus</a></i> discovered in a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Maastricht" title="Maastricht" id="mwjQ">Maastricht</a> limestone quarry, 1770 (contemporary engraving)</figcaption></figure>

<p id="mwjg">It was not until the beginning of the 19th century that it became clear that reptiles and amphibians are, in fact, quite different animals, and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pierre_André_Latreille" title="Pierre André Latreille" id="mwjw">P.A. Latreille</a> erected the class <i id="mwkA">Batracia</i> (1825) for the latter, dividing the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Tetrapod" title="Tetrapod" id="mwkQ">tetrapods</a> into the four familiar classes of reptiles, amphibians, birds, and mammals.<sup about="#mwt71" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-9" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-9"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-9" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 9;" id="mwkg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwkw">[9]</span></a></sup> The British anatomist <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Thomas_Henry_Huxley" title="Thomas Henry Huxley" id="mwlA">T.H. Huxley</a> made Latreille's definition popular and, together with <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Richard_Owen" title="Richard Owen" id="mwlQ">Richard Owen</a>, expanded Reptilia to include the various fossil "<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Antediluvian" title="Antediluvian" id="mwlg">antediluvian</a> monsters", including <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur" id="mwlw">dinosaurs</a> and the mammal-like (<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Synapsid" title="Synapsid" id="mwmA">synapsid</a>) <i id="mwmQ"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dicynodon" title="Dicynodon" id="mwmg">Dicynodon</a></i> he helped describe. This was not the only possible classification scheme: In the Hunterian lectures delivered at the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Royal_College_of_Surgeons_of_England" title="Royal College of Surgeons of England" id="mwmw">Royal College of Surgeons</a> in 1863, Huxley grouped the vertebrates into <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mammal" title="Mammal" id="mwnA">mammals</a>, sauroids, and ichthyoids (the latter containing the fishes and amphibians). He subsequently proposed the names of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sauropsida" title="Sauropsida" id="mwnQ">Sauropsida</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ichthyopsida" title="Ichthyopsida" class="mw-redirect" id="mwng">Ichthyopsida</a> for the latter two groups.<sup about="#mwt75" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-10" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-10"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-10" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 10;" id="mwnw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwoA">[10]</span></a></sup> In 1866, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ernst_Haeckel" title="Ernst Haeckel" id="mwoQ">Haeckel</a> demonstrated that vertebrates could be divided based on their reproductive strategies, and that reptiles, birds, and mammals were united by the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Amniotic_egg" title="Amniotic egg" class="mw-redirect" id="mwog">amniotic egg</a>.</p>

<p id="mwow">The terms <i id="mwpA">Sauropsida</i> ("lizard faces") and <i id="mwpQ"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Synapsid" title="Synapsid" id="mwpg">Theropsida</a></i> ("beast faces") were used again in 1916 by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Edwin_Stephen_Goodrich" title="Edwin Stephen Goodrich" id="mwpw">E.S. Goodrich</a> to distinguish between lizards, birds, and their relatives on the one hand (Sauropsida) and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mammal" title="Mammal" id="mwqA">mammals</a> and their extinct relatives (Theropsida) on the other. Goodrich supported this division by the nature of the hearts and blood vessels in each group, and other features, such as the structure of the forebrain. According to Goodrich, both lineages evolved from an earlier stem group, Protosauria ("first lizards") in which he included some animals today considered <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Reptiliomorpha" title="Reptiliomorpha" id="mwqQ">reptile-like amphibians</a>, as well as early reptiles.<sup about="#mwt80" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-goodrich1916_11-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"goodrich1916"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-goodrich1916-11"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-goodrich1916-11" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 11;" id="mwqg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwqw">[11]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwrA">In 1956, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./D._M._S._Watson" title="D. M. S. Watson" id="mwrQ">D.M.S. Watson</a> observed that the first two groups diverged very early in reptilian history, so he divided Goodrich's Protosauria between them. He also reinterpreted Sauropsida and Theropsida to exclude birds and mammals, respectively. Thus his Sauropsida included <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Procolophonia" title="Procolophonia" id="mwrg">Procolophonia</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Eosuchia" title="Eosuchia" id="mwrw">Eosuchia</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Millerettid" title="Millerettid" class="mw-redirect" id="mwsA">Millerosauria</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Turtle" title="Turtle" id="mwsQ">Chelonia</a> (turtles), <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Squamata" title="Squamata" id="mwsg">Squamata</a> (lizards and snakes), <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sphenodontia" title="Sphenodontia" class="mw-redirect" id="mwsw">Rhynchocephalia</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crocodilia" title="Crocodilia" id="mwtA">Crocodilia</a>, "<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Thecodontia" title="Thecodontia" id="mwtQ">thecodonts</a>" (<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Paraphyly" title="Paraphyly" id="mwtg">paraphyletic</a> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Basal_(phylogenetics)" title="Basal (phylogenetics)" id="mwtw">basal</a> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Archosaur" title="Archosaur" id="mwuA">Archosauria</a>), non-<a rel="mw:WikiLink/Interwiki" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/avian" title="wikt:avian" class="extiw" id="mwuQ">avian</a> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur" id="mwug">dinosaurs</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pterosaur" title="Pterosaur" id="mwuw">pterosaurs</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ichthyosaur" title="Ichthyosaur" id="mwvA">ichthyosaurs</a>, and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sauropterygia" title="Sauropterygia" id="mwvQ">sauropterygians</a>.<sup about="#mwt85" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-watson1956_12-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"watson1956"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-watson1956-12"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-watson1956-12" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 12;" id="mwvg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwvw">[12]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwwA">In the late 19th century, a number of definitions of Reptilia were offered. The traits listed by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Richard_Lydekker" title="Richard Lydekker" id="mwwQ">Lydekker</a> in 1896, for example, include a single <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Occipital_condyle" title="Occipital condyle" class="mw-redirect" id="mwwg">occipital condyle</a>, a jaw joint formed by the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Quadrate_bone" title="Quadrate bone" id="mwww">quadrate</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Articular" title="Articular" class="mw-redirect" id="mwxA">articular</a> bones, and certain characteristics of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vertebral_column" title="Vertebral column" id="mwxQ">vertebrae</a>.<sup about="#mwt91" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-13" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-13"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-13" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 13;" id="mwxg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwxw">[13]</span></a></sup> The animals singled out by these formulations, the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Amniote" title="Amniote" id="mwyA">amniotes</a> other than the mammals and the birds, are still those considered reptiles today.<sup about="#mwt92" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-tudge_14-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"tudge"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-tudge-14" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 14;" id="mwyQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwyg">[14]</span></a></sup></p>

<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwyw"><a href="./File:Captorhinus_aguti_p.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwzA"><img resource="./File:Captorhinus_aguti_p.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Captorhinus_aguti_p.jpg/220px-Captorhinus_aguti_p.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="4575" data-file-height="3375" data-file-type="bitmap" height="162" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Captorhinus_aguti_p.jpg/330px-Captorhinus_aguti_p.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Captorhinus_aguti_p.jpg/440px-Captorhinus_aguti_p.jpg 2x" id="mwzQ"/></a><figcaption id="mwzg">The first reptiles had an <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Anapsid" title="Anapsid" id="mwzw">anapsid</a> type of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Skull_roof" title="Skull roof" id="mw0A">skull roof</a>, as seen in the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Permian" title="Permian" id="mw0Q">Permian</a> genus <i id="mw0g"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Captorhinus" title="Captorhinus" id="mw0w">Captorhinus</a></i></figcaption></figure>

<p id="mw1A">The synapsid/sauropsid division supplemented another approach, one that split the reptiles into four subclasses based on the number and position of <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Skull#Temporal_fenestra" title="Skull" id="mw1Q">temporal fenestrae</a>, openings in the sides of the skull behind the eyes. This classification was initiated by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Henry_Fairfield_Osborn" title="Henry Fairfield Osborn" id="mw1g">Henry Fairfield Osborn</a> and elaborated and made popular by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Alfred_Romer" title="Alfred Romer" id="mw1w">Romer</a>'s classic <i id="mw2A"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Vertebrate_Paleontology_(Romer)" title="Vertebrate Paleontology (Romer)" class="mw-redirect" id="mw2Q">Vertebrate Paleontology</a></i>.<sup about="#mwt98" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-15" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-15"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-15" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 15;" id="mw2g"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mw2w">[15]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt102" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-romer1933_16-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"romer1933"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-romer1933-16"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-romer1933-16" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 16;" id="mw3A"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mw3Q">[16]</span></a></sup> Those four subclasses were:</p>
<ul id="mw3g"><li id="mw3w"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Anapsid" title="Anapsid" id="mw4A">Anapsida</a> – no fenestrae – <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cotylosaur" title="Cotylosaur" class="mw-redirect" id="mw4Q">cotylosaurs</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Turtle" title="Turtle" id="mw4g">chelonia</a> (<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Turtle" title="Turtle" id="mw4w">turtles</a> and relatives)<sup about="#mwt103" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-17" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Transclusion mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"efn","href":"./Template:Efn"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"\nThis taxonomy does not reflect modern molecular evidence, which places turtles within [[Diapsida]].\n"}},"i":0}}]}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-17" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 1;" data-mw-group="lower-alpha" id="mw5A"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mw5Q">[lower-alpha 1]</span></a></sup></li>
<li id="mw5g"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Synapsid" title="Synapsid" id="mw5w">Synapsida</a> – one low fenestrum – <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pelycosaur" title="Pelycosaur" id="mw6A">pelycosaurs</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Therapsid" title="Therapsid" id="mw6Q">therapsids</a> (the '<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mammal-like_reptiles" title="Mammal-like reptiles" class="mw-redirect" id="mw6g">mammal-like reptiles</a>')</li>
<li id="mw6w"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Euryapsida" title="Euryapsida" id="mw7A">Euryapsida</a><span typeof="mw:Entity" id="mw7Q"> </span>– one high fenestra (above the postorbital and squamosal)<span typeof="mw:Entity" id="mw7g"> </span>– <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Protorosaur" title="Protorosaur" class="mw-redirect" id="mw7w">protorosaurs</a> (small, early lizard-like reptiles) and the marine <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sauropterygia" title="Sauropterygia" id="mw8A">sauropterygians</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ichthyosaurs" title="Ichthyosaurs" class="mw-redirect" id="mw8Q">ichthyosaurs</a>, the latter called <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Parapsida" title="Parapsida" class="mw-redirect" id="mw8g">Parapsida</a> in Osborn's work.</li>
<li id="mw8w"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Diapsid" title="Diapsid" id="mw9A">Diapsida</a> – two fenestrae – most reptiles, including <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lizard" title="Lizard" id="mw9Q">lizards</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Snake" title="Snake" id="mw9g">snakes</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crocodilian" title="Crocodilian" class="mw-redirect" id="mw9w">crocodilians</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur" id="mw-A">dinosaurs</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pterosaur" title="Pterosaur" id="mw-Q">pterosaurs</a></li></ul>

<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mw-g"><a href="./File:Varanodon1DB.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mw-w"><img resource="./File:Varanodon1DB.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Varanodon1DB.jpg/220px-Varanodon1DB.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="1700" data-file-height="958" data-file-type="bitmap" height="124" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Varanodon1DB.jpg/330px-Varanodon1DB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Varanodon1DB.jpg/440px-Varanodon1DB.jpg 2x" id="mw_A"/></a><figcaption id="mw_Q">Phylogenetic classifications group the traditional "mammal-like reptiles", like this <i id="mw_g"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Varanodon" title="Varanodon" id="mw_w">Varanodon</a></i>, with other synapsids, not with extant reptiles</figcaption></figure>
<p id="mwAQA">The composition of Euryapsida was uncertain. <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ichthyosaurs" title="Ichthyosaurs" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAQE">Ichthyosaurs</a> were, at times, considered to have arisen independently of the other euryapsids, and given the older name Parapsida. Parapsida was later discarded as a group for the most part (ichthyosaurs being classified as <i id="mwAQI"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Incertae_sedis" title="Incertae sedis" id="mwAQM">incertae sedis</a></i> or with Euryapsida). However, four (or three if Euryapsida is merged into Diapsida) subclasses remained more or less universal for non-specialist work throughout the 20th<span typeof="mw:Entity" id="mwAQQ"> </span>century. It has largely been abandoned by recent researchers: In particular, the anapsid condition has been found to occur so variably among unrelated groups that it is not now considered a useful distinction.<sup about="#mwt110" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-18" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-18"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-18" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 17;" id="mwAQU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAQY">[17]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="3" id="mwAQc"><h3 id="Phylogenetics_and_modern_definition">Phylogenetics and modern definition</h3>
<p id="mwAQg">By the early 21st century, vertebrate paleontologists were beginning to adopt <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Phylogenetic" title="Phylogenetic" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAQk">phylogenetic</a> taxonomy, in which all groups are defined in such a way as to be <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Clade" title="Clade" id="mwAQo">monophyletic</a>; that is, groups which include all descendants of a particular ancestor. The reptiles as historically defined are <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Paraphyly" title="Paraphyly" id="mwAQs">paraphyletic</a>, since they exclude both birds and mammals. These respectively evolved from dinosaurs and from early therapsids, both of which were traditionally called "reptiles".<sup about="#mwt115" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Brysse2008_19-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Brysse2008"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Brysse2008-19"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Brysse2008-19" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 18;" id="mwAQw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAQ0">[18]</span></a></sup> Birds are more closely related to <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crocodilian" title="Crocodilian" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAQ4">crocodilians</a> than the latter are to the rest of extant reptiles. <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Colin_Tudge" title="Colin Tudge" id="mwAQ8">Colin Tudge</a> wrote:</p>

<blockquote id="mwARA"><p id="mwARE">Mammals are a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Clade" title="Clade" id="mwARI">clade</a>, and therefore the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Phylogenetic_nomenclature" title="Phylogenetic nomenclature" id="mwARM">cladists</a> are happy to acknowledge the traditional taxon <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Mammal" title="Mammal" id="mwARQ">Mammalia</a>; and birds, too, are a clade, universally ascribed to the formal taxon <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Bird" title="Bird" id="mwARU">Aves</a>. Mammalia and Aves are, in fact, subclades within the grand clade of the Amniota. But the traditional class Reptilia is not a clade. It is just a section of the clade <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Amniota" title="Amniota" class="mw-redirect" id="mwARY">Amniota</a>: The section that is left after the Mammalia and Aves have been hived off. It cannot be defined by <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Synapomorphy" title="Synapomorphy" class="mw-redirect" id="mwARc">synapomorphies</a>, as is the proper way. Instead, it is defined by a combination of the features it has and the features it lacks: reptiles are the amniotes that lack fur or feathers. At best, the cladists suggest, we could say that the traditional Reptilia are 'non-avian, non-mammalian amniotes'.<sup about="#mwt120" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-tudge_14-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"tudge"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-tudge-14"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-tudge-14" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 14;" id="mwARg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwARk">[14]</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>

<p id="mwARo">Despite the early proposals for replacing the paraphyletic Reptilia with a monophyletic <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sauropsida" title="Sauropsida" id="mwARs">Sauropsida</a>, which includes birds, that term was never adopted widely or, when it was, was not applied consistently.<sup about="#mwt125" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-modestoanderson2004_20-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"modestoanderson2004"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-modestoanderson2004-20"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-modestoanderson2004-20" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 19;" id="mwARw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAR0">[19]</span></a></sup></p>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwAR4"><a href="./File:Bearded_Dragon_Skeleton.jpg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwAR8"><img resource="./File:Bearded_Dragon_Skeleton.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Bearded_Dragon_Skeleton.jpg/220px-Bearded_Dragon_Skeleton.jpg" decoding="async" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" data-file-type="bitmap" height="147" width="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Bearded_Dragon_Skeleton.jpg/330px-Bearded_Dragon_Skeleton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Bearded_Dragon_Skeleton.jpg/440px-Bearded_Dragon_Skeleton.jpg 2x" id="mwASA"/></a><figcaption id="mwASE">Bearded dragon (<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pogona" title="Pogona" id="mwASI">pogona</a>) skeleton on display at the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Museum_of_Osteology" title="Museum of Osteology" id="mwASM">Museum of Osteology</a></figcaption></figure>
<p id="mwASQ">When Sauropsida was used, it often had the same content or even the same definition as Reptilia. In 1988, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Jacques_Gauthier" title="Jacques Gauthier" id="mwASU">Jacques Gauthier</a> proposed a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cladistics" title="Cladistics" id="mwASY">cladistic</a> definition of Reptilia as a monophyletic node-based <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crown_group" title="Crown group" id="mwASc">crown group</a> containing turtles, lizards and snakes, crocodilians, and birds, their common ancestor and all its descendants. While Gauthier's definition was close to the modern consensus, nonetheless, it became considered inadequate because the actual relationship of turtles to other reptiles was not yet well understood at this time.<sup about="#mwt128" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-modestoanderson2004_20-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"modestoanderson2004"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-modestoanderson2004-20" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 19;" id="mwASg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwASk">[19]</span></a></sup> Major revisions since have included the reassignment of synapsids as non-reptiles, and classification of turtles as diapsids.<sup about="#mwt129" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-modestoanderson2004_20-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"modestoanderson2004"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-modestoanderson2004-20" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 19;" id="mwASo"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwASs">[19]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwASw">A variety of other definitions were proposed by other scientists in the years following Gauthier's paper. The first such new definition, which attempted to adhere to the standards of the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./PhyloCode" title="PhyloCode" id="mwAS0">PhyloCode</a>, was published by Modesto and Anderson in 2004.<sup about="#mwt132" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-modestoanderson2004_20-3" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"modestoanderson2004"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-modestoanderson2004-20" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 19;" id="mwAS4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAS8">[19]</span></a></sup> Modesto and Anderson reviewed the many previous definitions and proposed a modified definition, which they intended to retain most traditional content of the group while keeping it stable and monophyletic. They defined Reptilia as all amniotes closer to <i id="mwATA"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lacerta_agilis" title="Lacerta agilis" class="mw-redirect" id="mwATE">Lacerta agilis</a></i> and <i id="mwATI"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crocodylus_niloticus" title="Crocodylus niloticus" class="mw-redirect" id="mwATM">Crocodylus niloticus</a></i> than to <i id="mwATQ"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens" class="mw-redirect" id="mwATU">Homo sapiens</a></i>. This stem-based definition is equivalent to the more common definition of Sauropsida, which Modesto and Anderson synonymized with Reptilia, since the latter is better known and more frequently used. Unlike most previous definitions of Reptilia, however, Modesto and Anderson's definition includes birds, as they are within the clade that includes both lizards and crocodiles.<sup about="#mwt133" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-modestoanderson2004_20-4" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"modestoanderson2004"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-modestoanderson2004-20" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 19;" id="mwATY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwATc">[19]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="4" id="mwATg"><h3 id="Taxonomy">Taxonomy</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt134" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"See also","href":"./Template:See_also"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"List of reptiles"},"2":{"wt":"List of snakes"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwATk"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt134" id="mwATo">See also: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./List_of_reptiles" title="List of reptiles">List of reptiles</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./List_of_snakes" title="List of snakes" class="mw-redirect">List of snakes</a></div>
<p id="mwATs">General classification of extinct and living reptiles, focusing on major groups.<sup about="#mwt142" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-benton2005_21-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"benton2005"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-benton2005-21"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-benton2005-21" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 20;" id="mwATw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAT0">[20]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt146" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-benton2014_22-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"benton2014"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-benton2014-22"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-benton2014-22" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 21;" id="mwAT4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAT8">[21]</span></a></sup></p><!-- Note to editors: the nested infraclasses are as presented in Benton's 4th edition. Infraclass Diapsida contains Infraclass Neodiapsida, which contains infraclasses Archosauromorpha and Lepidosauromorpha, with the latter containing Infraclass Ichthyosauria within an unnamed Infrasubclass -->
<ul id="mwAUA"><li id="mwAUE"><b id="mwAUI">Reptilia</b>/<b id="mwAUM"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sauropsida" title="Sauropsida" id="mwAUQ">Sauropsida</a></b>
<ul id="mwAUU"><li id="mwAUY"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt147" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAUc">†</abbr><b id="mwAUg"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Parareptilia" title="Parareptilia" id="mwAUk">Parareptilia</a></b></li>
<li id="mwAUo"><b id="mwAUs"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Eureptilia" title="Eureptilia" id="mwAUw">Eureptilia</a></b>
<ul id="mwAU0"><li id="mwAU4"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt148" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAU8">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Captorhinidae" title="Captorhinidae" id="mwAVA">Captorhinidae</a></li>

<ul id="mwAVQ"><li id="mwAVU"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt149" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAVY">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Araeoscelidia" title="Araeoscelidia" id="mwAVc">Araeoscelidia</a></li>
<li id="mwAVg"><b id="mwAVk"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Neodiapsida" title="Neodiapsida" id="mwAVo">Neodiapsida</a></b>
<ul id="mwAVs"><li id="mwAVw"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt150" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAV0">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Drepanosauromorpha" title="Drepanosauromorpha" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAV4">Drepanosauromorpha</a> (placement uncertain)</li>
<li id="mwAV8"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt151" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAWA">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Younginiformes" title="Younginiformes" id="mwAWE">Younginiformes</a> (<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Paraphyletic" title="Paraphyletic" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAWI">paraphyletic</a>)</li>
<li id="mwAWM"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt152" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAWQ">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ichthyosauromorpha" title="Ichthyosauromorpha" id="mwAWU">Ichthyosauromorpha</a> (placement uncertain)</li>
<li id="mwAWY"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt153" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAWc">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Thalattosauria" title="Thalattosauria" id="mwAWg">Thalattosauria</a> (placement uncertain)</li>
<li id="mwAWk"><b id="mwAWo"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sauria" title="Sauria" id="mwAWs">Sauria</a></b>
<ul id="mwAWw"><li id="mwAW0"><b id="mwAW4"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lepidosauromorpha" title="Lepidosauromorpha" id="mwAW8">Lepidosauromorpha</a></b>
<ul id="mwAXA"><li id="mwAXE"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Lepidosauriformes" title="Lepidosauriformes" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAXI">Lepidosauriformes</a>
<ul id="mwAXM"><li id="mwAXQ"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Rhynchocephalia" title="Rhynchocephalia" id="mwAXU">Rhynchocephalia</a> (tuatara)</li>
<li id="mwAXY"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Squamata" title="Squamata" id="mwAXc">Squamata</a> (lizards &amp; snakes)</li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li id="mwAXg"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt154" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAXk">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Choristodera" title="Choristodera" id="mwAXo">Choristodera</a> (placement uncertain)</li>
<li id="mwAXs"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt155" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAXw">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Sauropterygia" title="Sauropterygia" id="mwAX0">Sauropterygia</a> (placement uncertain)</li>
<li id="mwAX4"><b id="mwAX8"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pantestudines" title="Pantestudines" id="mwAYA">Pantestudines</a></b> (turtles and kin, placement uncertain)</li>
<li id="mwAYE"><b id="mwAYI"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Archosauromorpha" title="Archosauromorpha" id="mwAYM">Archosauromorpha</a></b>
<ul id="mwAYQ"><li id="mwAYU"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt156" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAYY">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Protorosauria" title="Protorosauria" id="mwAYc">Protorosauria</a> (paraphyletic)</li>
<li id="mwAYg"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt157" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAYk">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Rhynchosauria" title="Rhynchosauria" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAYo">Rhynchosauria</a></li>
<li id="mwAYs"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt158" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAYw">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Allokotosauria" title="Allokotosauria" id="mwAY0">Allokotosauria</a></li>
<li id="mwAY4"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Archosauriformes" title="Archosauriformes" id="mwAY8">Archosauriformes</a>
<ul id="mwAZA"><li id="mwAZE"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt159" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAZI">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Phytosaur" title="Phytosaur" id="mwAZM">Phytosauria</a></li>
<li id="mwAZQ"><b id="mwAZU"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Archosauria" title="Archosauria" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAZY">Archosauria</a></b>
<ul id="mwAZc"><li id="mwAZg"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pseudosuchia" title="Pseudosuchia" id="mwAZk">Pseudosuchia</a>
<ul id="mwAZo"><li id="mwAZs"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crocodilia" title="Crocodilia" id="mwAZw">Crocodilia</a> (crocodilians)</li></ul></li>
<li id="mwAZ0"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Avemetatarsalia" title="Avemetatarsalia" id="mwAZ4">Avemetatarsalia</a>/<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ornithodira" title="Ornithodira" class="mw-redirect" id="mwAZ8">Ornithodira</a>
<ul id="mwAaA"><li id="mwAaE"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt160" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAaI">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pterosaur" title="Pterosaur" id="mwAaM">Pterosauria</a></li>
<li id="mwAaQ"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Dinosaur" title="Dinosaur" id="mwAaU">Dinosauria</a>
<ul id="mwAaY"><li id="mwAac"><abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" about="#mwt161" typeof="mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"extinct","href":"./Template:Extinct"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwAag">†</abbr><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Ornithischia" title="Ornithischia" id="mwAak">Ornithischia</a></li>
<li id="mwAao"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Saurischia" title="Saurischia" id="mwAas">Saurischia</a> (including birds (<b id="mwAaw"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Bird" title="Bird" id="mwAa0">Aves</a></b>))</li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="5" id="mwAa4"><h3 id="Phylogeny">Phylogeny</h3>
<p id="mwAa8">The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cladistics#Cladograms" title="Cladistics" id="mwAbA">cladogram</a> presented here illustrates the "family tree" of reptiles, and follows a simplified version of the relationships found by M.S. Lee, in 2013.<sup about="#mwt174" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-scaffold2013_23-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"scaffold2013"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-scaffold2013-23"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-scaffold2013-23" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 22;" id="mwAbE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAbI">[22]</span></a></sup> All <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Molecular_phylogenetics" title="Molecular phylogenetics" id="mwAbM">genetic</a> studies have supported the hypothesis that turtles are diapsids; some have placed turtles within Archosauromorpha,<sup about="#mwt175" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-scaffold2013_23-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"scaffold2013"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-scaffold2013-23" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 22;" id="mwAbQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAbU">[22]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt179" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Mannen_24-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Mannen"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Mannen-24"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Mannen-24" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 23;" id="mwAbY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAbc">[23]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt180" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Zardoya_25-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Zardoya"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Zardoya-25" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 24;" id="mwAbg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAbk">[24]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt181" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Iwabe_26-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Iwabe"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Iwabe-26" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 25;" id="mwAbo"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAbs">[25]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt182" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Roos_27-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Roos"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Roos-27" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 26;" id="mwAbw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAb0">[26]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt183" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Katsu_28-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Katsu"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Katsu-28" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 27;" id="mwAb4"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAb8">[27]</span></a></sup> though a few have recovered turtles as Lepidosauromorpha instead.<sup about="#mwt187" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-29" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-29"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-29" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 28;" id="mwAcA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAcE">[28]</span></a></sup> The cladogram below used a combination of genetic (molecular) and fossil (morphological) data to obtain its results.<sup about="#mwt188" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-scaffold2013_23-2" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"scaffold2013"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-scaffold2013-23" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 22;" id="mwAcI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwAcM">[22]</span></a></sup></p>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1129740115" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" about="#mwt189"
