<p id="mwBcE">The turtle has a prominent position as a symbol of steadfastness and tranquility in religion, mythology, and folklore from around the world.<sup about="#mwt999" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Plotkin_157-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Plotkin"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Plotkin-157"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Plotkin-157" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 154;" id="mwBcI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBcM">[154]</span></a></sup> A tortoise's longevity is suggested by its long lifespan and its shell, which was thought to protect it from any foe.<sup about="#mwt1003" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Ball_158-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Ball"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Ball-158"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Ball-158" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 155;" id="mwBcQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBcU">[155]</span></a></sup> In the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cosmological_myth" title="Cosmological myth" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBcY">cosmological myths</a> of several cultures a <i id="mwBcc"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./World_Turtle" title="World Turtle" id="mwBcg">World Turtle</a></i> carries the world upon its back or supports the heavens.<sup about="#mwt1007" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Stookey_159-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Stookey"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Stookey-159"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Stookey-159" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 156;" id="mwBck"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBco">[156]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="36" id="mwBcs"><h3 id="Medicine">Medicine</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt1008" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"See also","href":"./Template:See_also"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Epidemiology of snakebites"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBcw"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt1008" id="mwBc0">See also: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Epidemiology_of_snakebites" title="Epidemiology of snakebites">Epidemiology of snakebites</a></div><figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb" id="mwBc4"><a href="./File:Rod_of_Asclepius2.svg" class="mw-file-description" id="mwBc8"><img resource="./File:Rod_of_Asclepius2.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Rod_of_Asclepius2.svg/60px-Rod_of_Asclepius2.svg.png" decoding="async" data-file-width="251" data-file-height="804" data-file-type="drawing" height="192" width="60" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Rod_of_Asclepius2.svg/90px-Rod_of_Asclepius2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Rod_of_Asclepius2.svg/120px-Rod_of_Asclepius2.svg.png 2x" id="mwBdA"/></a><figcaption id="mwBdE">The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Rod_of_Asclepius" title="Rod of Asclepius" id="mwBdI">Rod of Asclepius</a> symbolizes medicine</figcaption></figure>
<p id="mwBdM">Deaths from <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Snakebite" title="Snakebite" id="mwBdQ">snakebites</a> are uncommon in many parts of the world, but are still counted in tens of thousands per year in India.<sup about="#mwt1017" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Sinha_160-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Sinha"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Sinha-160"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Sinha-160" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 157;" id="mwBdU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBdY">[157]</span></a></sup> Snakebite can be treated with <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Antivenom" title="Antivenom" id="mwBdc">antivenom</a> made from the venom of the snake. To produce antivenom, a mixture of the venoms of different species of snake is injected into the body of a horse in ever-increasing dosages until the horse is immunized. Blood is then extracted; the serum is separated, purified and freeze-dried.<sup about="#mwt1021" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-161" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-161"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-161" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 158;" id="mwBdg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBdk">[158]</span></a></sup> The <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Cytotoxic" title="Cytotoxic" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBdo">cytotoxic</a> effect of snake venom is being researched as a potential treatment for cancers.<sup about="#mwt1025" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-162" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-162"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-162" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 159;" id="mwBds"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBdw">[159]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBd0">Lizards such as the Gila monster produce toxins with medical applications. Gila toxin reduces plasma glucose; the substance is now synthesised for use in the anti-<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Diabetes" title="Diabetes" id="mwBd4">diabetes</a> drug <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Exenatide" title="Exenatide" id="mwBd8">exenatide</a> (Byetta).<sup about="#mwt1031" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Casey2013_163-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Casey2013"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Casey2013-163"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Casey2013-163" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 160;" id="mwBeA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBeE">[160]</span></a></sup> Another toxin from Gila monster saliva has been studied for use as an anti-<a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Alzheimer's" title="Alzheimer's" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBeI">Alzheimer's</a> drug.<sup about="#mwt1035" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-164" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-164"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-164" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 161;" id="mwBeM"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBeQ">[161]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBeU">Geckos have also been used as medicine, especially in China.<sup about="#mwt1042" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-165" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-165"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-165" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 162;" id="mwBeY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBec">[162]</span></a></sup> Turtles have been used in Chinese traditional medicine for thousands of years, with every part of the turtle believed to have medical benefits. There is a lack of scientific evidence that would correlate claimed medical benefits to turtle consumption. Growing demand for turtle meat has placed pressure on vulnerable wild populations of turtles.<sup about="#mwt1046" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-MongabayNews-2014-08-08_166-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"MongabayNews-2014-08-08"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-MongabayNews-2014-08-08-166"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-MongabayNews-2014-08-08-166" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 163;" id="mwBeg"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBek">[163]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="37" id="mwBeo"><h3 id="Commercial_farming">Commercial farming</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt1047" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"See also","href":"./Template:See_also"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Crocodile farm"},"2":{"wt":"Snake farm"},"3":{"wt":"Turtle farming"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBes"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt1047" id="mwBew">See also: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crocodile_farm" title="Crocodile farm">Crocodile farm</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Snake_farm" title="Snake farm">Snake farm</a>, and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Turtle_farming" title="Turtle farming">Turtle farming</a></div>
<p id="mwBe0">Crocodiles are protected in many parts of the world, and are <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crocodile_farm" title="Crocodile farm" id="mwBe4">farmed commercially</a>. Their hides are tanned and used to make leather goods such as shoes and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Handbag" title="Handbag" id="mwBe8">handbags</a>; crocodile meat is also considered a delicacy.<sup about="#mwt1055" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-167" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-167"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-167" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 164;" id="mwBfA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBfE">[164]</span></a></sup> The most commonly farmed species are the saltwater and Nile crocodiles. Farming has resulted in an increase in the saltwater crocodile population in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Australia" title="Australia" id="mwBfI">Australia</a>, as eggs are usually harvested from the wild, so landowners have an incentive to conserve their habitat. Crocodile leather is made into wallets, briefcases, purses, handbags, belts, hats, and shoes. <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Crocodile_oil" title="Crocodile oil" id="mwBfM">Crocodile oil</a> has been used for various purposes.<sup about="#mwt1059" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-168" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-168"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-168" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 165;" id="mwBfQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBfU">[165]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBfY">Snakes are also farmed, primarily in <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./East_Asia" title="East Asia" id="mwBfc">East</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia" id="mwBfg">Southeast Asia</a>, and their production has become more intensive in the last decade. <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Snake_farm" title="Snake farm" id="mwBfk">Snake farming</a> has been troubling for conservation in the past as it can lead to <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Overexploitation" title="Overexploitation" id="mwBfo">overexploitation</a> of wild snakes and their natural prey to supply the farms. However,  farming snakes can limit the hunting of wild snakes, while reducing the slaughter of higher-order vertebrates like cows. The energy efficiency of snakes is higher than expected for carnivores, due to their ectothermy and low metabolism. Waste protein from the poultry and pig industries is used as feed in snake farms.<sup about="#mwt1064" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-169" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-169"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-169" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 166;" id="mwBfs"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBfw">[166]</span></a></sup> Snake farms produce meat, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Snakeskin" title="Snakeskin" id="mwBf0">snake skin</a>, and antivenom.</p>

<p id="mwBf4"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Turtle_farming" title="Turtle farming" id="mwBf8">Turtle farming</a> is another known but controversial practice. Turtles have been farmed for a variety of reasons, ranging from food to traditional medicine, the pet trade, and scientific conservation. Demand for turtle meat and medicinal products is one of the main threats to turtle conservation in Asia. Though commercial breeding would seem to insulate wild populations, it can stoke the demand for them and increase wild captures.<sup about="#mwt1072" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-170" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-170"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-170" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 167;" id="mwBgA"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBgE">[167]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt1073" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-MongabayNews-2014-08-08_166-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"MongabayNews-2014-08-08"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-MongabayNews-2014-08-08-166" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 163;" id="mwBgI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBgM">[163]</span></a></sup> Even the potentially appealing concept of raising turtles at a farm to release into the wild is questioned by some veterinarians who have had some experience with farm operations. They caution that this may introduce into the wild populations infectious diseases that occur on the farm, but have not (yet) been occurring in the wild.<sup about="#mwt1077" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-171" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-171"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-171" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 168;" id="mwBgQ"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBgU">[168]</span></a></sup><sup about="#mwt1081" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-172" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-172"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-172" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 169;" id="mwBgY"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBgc">[169]</span></a></sup></p>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="38" id="mwBgg"><h3 id="Reptiles_in_captivity">Reptiles in captivity</h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" about="#mwt1082" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"further","href":"./Template:Further"},"params":{"1":{"wt":"Herpetoculture"}},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBgk"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" about="#mwt1082" id="mwBgo">Further information: <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Herpetoculture" title="Herpetoculture">Herpetoculture</a></div>
<p id="mwBgs">A <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Herpetarium" title="Herpetarium" id="mwBgw">herpetarium</a> is a <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Zoo" title="Zoo" id="mwBg0">zoological exhibition</a> space for reptiles and amphibians.</p>

<p id="mwBg4">In the Western world, some snakes (especially relatively docile species such as the <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Python_regius" title="Python regius" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBg8">ball python</a> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Corn_snake" title="Corn snake" id="mwBhA">corn snake</a>) are sometimes kept as pets.<sup about="#mwt1092" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-173" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-173"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-173" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 170;" id="mwBhE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBhI">[170]</span></a></sup> Numerous species of lizard are kept as <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pet" title="Pet" id="mwBhM">pets</a>, including <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Pogona" title="Pogona" id="mwBhQ">bearded dragons</a>,<sup about="#mwt1096" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Virata_174-0" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Virata"},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-Virata-174"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Virata-174" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 171;" id="mwBhU"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBhY">[171]</span></a></sup> <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Iguana" title="Iguana" id="mwBhc">iguanas</a>, <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Anole" title="Anole" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBhg">anoles</a>,<sup about="#mwt1100" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-175" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-175"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-175" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 172;" id="mwBhk"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBho">[172]</span></a></sup> and <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Gecko" title="Gecko" id="mwBhs">geckos</a> (such as the popular <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Leopard_gecko" title="Leopard gecko" id="mwBhw">leopard gecko</a> and the crested gecko).<sup about="#mwt1101" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-Virata_174-1" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{"name":"Virata"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-Virata-174" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 171;" id="mwBh0"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBh4">[171]</span></a></sup></p>

<p id="mwBh8">Turtles and tortoises are increasingly popular pets, but keeping them can be challenging due to their particular requirements, such as temperature control, the need for UV light sources, and a varied diet. The long lifespans of turtles and especially tortoises mean they can potentially outlive their owners. Good hygiene and significant maintenance is necessary when keeping reptiles, due to the risks of <i id="mwBiA"><a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Salmonella" title="Salmonella" id="mwBiE">Salmonella</a></i> and other pathogens.<sup about="#mwt1106" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-176" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-176"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-176" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 173;" id="mwBiI"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBiM">[173]</span></a></sup> Regular hand-washing after handling is an important measure to prevent infection.</p>

</section></section><section data-mw-section-id="39" id="mwBiQ"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2>

</section><section data-mw-section-id="40" id="mwBi8"><h2 id="Further_reading">Further reading</h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1054258005" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" about="#mwt1108" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"refbegin","href":"./Template:Refbegin"},"params":{},"i":0}},"\n* ",{"template":{"target":{"wt":"cite book\n Vertebrates"},"edition":{"wt":"2nd"},"publisher":{"wt":"John Wiley and Sons Inc."},"location":{"wt":"New York, </section><section data-mw-section-id="41" id="mwBjI"><h2 id="Notes">Notes</h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734" typeof="mw:Extension/templatestyles mw:Transclusion" about="#mwt1124" data-mw='{"parts":[{"template":{"target":{"wt":"notelist","href":"./Template:Notelist"},"params":{},"i":0}}]}' id="mwBjM">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist  reflist-lower-alpha " about="#mwt1124" id="mwBjQ">
<div class="mw-references-wrap" typeof="mw:Extension/references" about="#mwt1128" data-mw='{"name":"references","attrs":{"group":"lower-alpha","responsive":"1"},"body":{"html":""}}' id="mwBjU"><ol class="mw-references references" data-mw-group="lower-alpha" id="mwBjY"><li about="#cite_note-17" id="cite_note-17"><a href="./Reptile#cite_ref-17" data-mw-group="lower-alpha" rel="mw:referencedBy" id="mwBjc"><span class="mw-linkback-text" id="mwBjg">↑ </span></a> <span id="mw-reference-text-cite_note-17" class="mw-reference-text">
This taxonomy does not reflect modern molecular evidence, which places turtles within <a rel="mw:WikiLink" href="./Diapsida" title="Diapsida" class="mw-redirect" id="mwBjk">Diapsida</a>.
</span></li><li about="#cite_note-123" id="cite_note-123"><a href="./Reptile#cite_ref-123" data-mw-group="lower-alpha" rel="mw:referencedBy" id="mwBjo"><span class="mw-linkback-text" id="mwBjs">↑ </span></a> <span id="mw-reference-text-cite_note-123" class="mw-reference-text">
"The copperhead is a pit viper and, like others pit vipers, it has heat-sensitive pit organs on each side of its head between the eye and the nostril. These pits detect objects that are warmer than the environment and enable copperheads to locate nocturnal, mammalian prey."<sup about="#mwt809" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-122" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-122"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-122" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 121;" id="mwBjw"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBj0">[121]</span></a></sup>
</span></li><li about="#cite_note-150" id="cite_note-150"><a href="./Reptile#cite_ref-150" data-mw-group="lower-alpha" rel="mw:referencedBy" id="mwBj4"><span class="mw-linkback-text" id="mwBj8">↑ </span></a> <span id="mw-reference-text-cite_note-150" class="mw-reference-text">
"Michaelmas term lately over, and the Lord Chancellor sitting in Lincoln's Inn Hall. Implacable November weather. As much mud in the streets, as if the waters had but newly retired from the face of the earth, and it would not be wonderful to meet a <i id="mwBkA">Megalosaurus</i>, forty feet long or so, waddling like an elephantine lizard up Holborne Hill."<sup about="#mwt953" class="mw-ref reference" id="cite_ref-149" rel="dc:references" typeof="mw:Extension/ref" data-mw='{"name":"ref","attrs":{},"body":{"id":"mw-reference-text-cite_note-149"}}'><a href="./Reptile#cite_note-149" style="counter-reset: mw-Ref 147;" id="mwBkE"><span class="mw-reflink-text" id="mwBkI">[147]</span></a></sup>
</span></li></ol></div></div>
